# iHYPE Design Sync Workflow
# ──────────────────────────────────────────────────────────
# How each design iteration flows from Claude Design → ihype.org
#
# PIPELINE:
#   Claude Design (.dc.html) → GitHub (src/app/*.tsx) → Cloudflare → ihype.org
#
# AGENTS:
#   Claude Design  — owns .dc.html files + design system
#   Claude Code    — owns src/app/ + API + database
#   Both           — read this file to stay in sync

---

## Step 1 · Design changes in Claude Design

When a page is updated, this file is edited:
  - DESIGN_SYNC.md → add entry to [PENDING CHANGES] below
  - .dc.html page updated
  - Ready for Claude Code to implement

---

## Step 2 · Claude Code reads DESIGN_SYNC.md

Claude Code checks [PENDING CHANGES] and for each entry:
  1. Opens the .dc.html URL listed
  2. Translates HTML/CSS/JS → Next.js page + components
  3. Wires the API calls listed under each change
  4. Marks the entry as [DONE] with commit SHA

---

## Step 3 · GitHub → Cloudflare → ihype.org (automatic)

  git push origin main
  → GitHub Actions: deploy-production.yml runs
  → OpenNext builds → Cloudflare Workers deploys
  → Live at ihype.org within ~2 minutes

---

| Email.dc.html        | — email templates —        | src/lib/email/templates/        |

### ⚠ Route-ownership resolutions
**Updated 2026-06-30 (v2) — supersedes earlier legal-split decision:**
- **Legal.dc.html is the single CANONICAL legal page** with three in-page tabs (Privacy · Terms · Charter) serving `/legal`, `/privacy`, and `/terms`. Standalone `Privacy.dc.html` and `Terms.dc.html` were **DELETED** (redundant) — their content is merged into Legal's tabs. Charter also keeps its standalone `/charter` page (Charter.dc.html). Route `/privacy` and `/terms` to Legal (deep-link the matching tab).
- **`Radio.dc.html` (DJ Studio) DELETED** — superseded by WebRadio.dc.html, which now owns `/radio`. DJ go-live / schedule / manage / edit actions repointed to **Studio.dc.html** (creator workbench). If a dedicated DJ broadcast console is needed later, add it as a Studio tab, not a separate page.
- **`Discover.dc.html` DELETED** — redundant with Search + Charts + Seeds (FanHome). Its links were removed from Sitemap.
- **404 vs Offline** — unchanged: 404.dc.html → `not-found.tsx`; Offline.dc.html → `error.tsx`/`global-error.tsx` + `/offline`.
- **Global footer** — NavShell now injects a fixed footer bar (Legal | Support | © 2026 ihype.org) on every page; header + footer are solid (no transparency/blur).

## Design Token Map · DS → Next.js globals.css

Claude Code: copy these into src/app/globals.css

```css
/* iHYPE Design Tokens — auto-synced from DS 39bcce7b */

:root {
  /* Backgrounds */
  --bg:  #0a0805;
  --bg2: #100d09;
  --bg3: #1a1611;
  --bg4: #241d18;

  /* Text */
  --ink:  #f0ebe5;
  --line: rgba(255, 255, 255, 0.06);

  /* Brand */
  --accent:    #ff5029;   /* iHYPE orange-red */

  /* Roles */
  --fan:       #b983ff;   /* purple */
  --venue:     #22e5d4;   /* teal */
  --promoter:  #ff3e9a;   /* pink */
  --artist:    #ff5029;   /* same as accent */

  /* Typography */
  --font-display: 'Syne', sans-serif;         /* 800 weight only */
  --font-body:    'DM Sans', sans-serif;       /* 400/500 */
  --font-mono:    'JetBrains Mono', monospace; /* labels, ALL CAPS */
  --font-serif:   'Instrument Serif', serif;   /* italic, editorial */

  /* Radius */
  --radius-sm:  8px;
  --radius-md:  10px;
  --radius-lg:  24px;
  --radius-xl:  32px;
  --radius-pill: 9999px;

  /* Motion */
  --ease-spring: cubic-bezier(0.2, 0.7, 0.3, 1);
  --duration-fast: 150ms;
  --duration-base: 200ms;
  --duration-slow: 300ms;
}
```

---

## API Client · lib/api.js → src/lib/api.ts

Claude Code: the design API client (lib/api.js) maps 1:1 to the Next.js API routes.
For server components, use `db.*` directly. For client components, use fetch or SWR.

```typescript
// Pattern used in all .dc.html pages:
const shows = await API.events.list({ city: 'San Francisco' });

// Next.js server component equivalent:
const shows = await db.event.findMany({
  where: { city: 'San Francisco', status: 'PUBLISHED' },
  orderBy: { startsAt: 'asc' }
});
```

---

## API ALIGNMENT & GAPS · reconciled against lib/api.js (2026-06-30)

**Authoritative:** `lib/api.js` is the real client surface. Earlier RECONCILE rows (20–42) carried *guessed* endpoints — use the table below instead. Endpoints marked **GAP** do not exist in `lib/api.js` yet; Claude Code must add them to **both** `lib/api.js` (design) and `src/app/api/*` (backend) so the two sides line up when merged. Until a GAP is filled, the page runs on `MOCK` fallback.

| Studio #2 | `API.events.create()` · `API.me.earnings()` · `API.hype.charts()` | — |

### Consolidated GAP list — add to lib/api.js AND src/app/api (both agents)
1. `GET /fans/:slug` → `API.fans.get(slug)` — public fan profile
2. `GET /me/notifications` + `POST /notifications/:id/read` → `API.notifications.list()` / `.markRead(id)`
3. `GET /payout/:eventId` → `API.payouts.get(eventId)` — post-event receipt (45/45/10)
4. `POST /verify` → `API.verify.submit(data)` — applicant proof submission (distinct from admin review)
5. `POST /beta/join` → `API.beta.join(email)` — TestFlight waitlist
6. `GET /radio-shows/:id/replay` → `API.radio.replay(id)` + live/record: `POST /radio/live`, `POST /radio/record`
7. `GET /artists/:slug/radio-archive` → `API.artists.radioArchive(slug)` — DJ show archive

> **Merge rule:** a GAP endpoint must be added to `lib/api.js` in the SAME change that implements the page's `.tsx`, and the route must exist under `src/app/api/`. Add each new method to the "API Client" 1:1 map above so the design ↔ backend surfaces never drift again.

---

1. **Design is source of truth for:** layout, copy, colors, component structure
2. **Code is source of truth for:** data shapes, auth logic, business rules
3. **Never diverge on:** 45/45/10 split, $0 fees copy, role colors
4. **Always sync on:** major layout changes, new pages, removed features

---

## PENDING CHANGES
<!-- Claude Design adds entries here. Claude Code marks them [DONE]. -->

| # | Page | What Changed | API Calls | Status |
|---|------|-------------|-----------|--------|
| 230 | (no `.dc.html` — closes a documented scope gap from row 226) | **DJ Dashboard now surfaces lineup bookings on other venues' shows.** Row 226 (Lineup & Split Agreement) explicitly flagged this as a known gap: a DJ booked as a lineup act on someone else's venue-booked show got a real notification, but their own `/promoters/[slug]/dashboard` "Upcoming Shows" list only ever queried `promoterProfileId: profile.id` (shows *they* promote/host), so the booking never showed up there. The query now also matches `lineupSlots: { some: { profileId } }`, includes `DRAFT` status (a lineup-pending show stays DRAFT until every act accepts), and the row links to `/shows/[slug]/lineup` for DRAFT shows with a "Lineup invite — review split" / "Booked as lineup act" meta line distinguishing it from the DJ's own hosted shows. | (query-only change, no new endpoint) | ✅ Done (code) |
| 229 | Advertise.dc.html's existing "3rd-Party Accounts" copy (new `/advertise/register` route, not a new template) | **Advertiser Profile — a real, separate 5th account type, per explicit user request** ("Create an advertiser profile separate from the main 4 so non app users can manage their advertising campaigns"). Advertise.dc.html already described this exact concept in its live "Two ways in" section (Members vs. "3rd-Party Accounts" — music stores, merch printers, live-production companies) but the "Open a 3rd-party account →" CTA was a dead anchor link; there was no actual account type to open. Per explicit product decisions (private-only, no public profile page; a brand-new dedicated signup flow rather than a 5th option on `/register`): added `Role.ADVERTISER` (migration `20260719120000_add_advertiser_role_and_account`, applied live) and a new `AdvertiserAccount` model (`companyName`/`contactName`/`website`, 1:1 with `User`) — deliberately NOT a `ProfileType`/`Profile` row, since advertisers have no public-facing page and none of `Profile`'s public-profile fields apply. New `POST /api/advertise/register` creates the `User`+`AdvertiserAccount` (no music-industry fields, no invite code, no Profile) and sends a real sign-in link via the **existing passwordless magic-link mechanism already used everywhere in this app** (extracted the shared send logic into `src/lib/magic-link.ts`, reused by both the pre-existing `/api/auth/magic-link` and this new route — no new auth mechanism invented). `GET /api/auth/magic` now routes an `ADVERTISER` straight to `/advertise/dashboard` on first sign-in (same pattern as the existing `ADMIN` → `/admin` special case). `Ad.advertiserId` still points at `User` directly, completely untouched — an advertiser account works with the existing real campaign-submission/vetting pipeline with zero changes there. **Linked all advertising pages together**: `/advertise`'s "Open a 3rd-party account →" now really links to `/advertise/register`; added an "Already advertising? Go to your dashboard →" link in the hero; `/advertise/dashboard` now real-displays the signed-in advertiser's `companyName`/`website` when an `AdvertiserAccount` exists, and its login redirect now preserves `callbackUrl=/advertise/dashboard` (previously dropped it, landing back at a generic `/login`). Independently typechecked every touched/new file — zero new errors (the two `TS7053` hits in `AdvertisePage.tsx` pre-date this change, confirmed via `git diff`). | POST /api/advertise/register, GET /api/auth/magic (ADVERTISER redirect) | ✅ Done (code + migration applied live) |
| 228 | TrackDetail.dc.html, PayoutSettings.dc.html (new `templates/` tree; no template exists for support tickets) | **Three independent, lower-risk pages built via a 3-agent parallel workflow + verify pass.** (1) **Track Detail** — real public `/tracks/[hexId]` page (no auth, same pattern as a public artist profile), looked up by the same `hexId` `src/app/embed/[hexId]/route.ts` already uses. Real title/notes/duration from `ArtistMediaAsset`, real play count (`MediaListen` count), real "More from {Artist}" list, and a real per-track "Copyright status" line derived from the latest `ContentReport` for that track (not a hardcoded "Cleared"). The mock's "Hype" button implied a per-track hype counter that doesn't exist anywhere in the schema (only profile-level `ProfileHypeEvent` and show-level `HypeEvent`) — honestly relabeled to hype the *artist*, reusing the real existing `HypeButton`/`Profile.hypeCount` mechanism, with copy that says so rather than faking a track-level tally. Reused the existing `GlobalMediaPlayer` context for real playback instead of inventing new player logic; dropped "Add to playlist" (no public/unauthenticated playlist-add endpoint exists). (2) **Payout Settings** — real `/me/payout-settings` (auth-gated), listing every owned ARTIST/DJ/VENUE profile's real `stripeConnectAccountId`/`stripeConnectOnboarded` state with a genuine Connect/Reconnect button hitting the existing `POST /api/stripe/connect/onboard`, plus a link to the already-built `/me/payouts` history page. Deliberately did not build "Add another account" (no multi-Connect-account support exists), "Payout Schedule" (payouts already run automatically via the real cron with no batching option), or "Email me on payout" (the cron already unconditionally emails on every transfer, no per-user toggle exists anywhere) — each omitted with an inline comment, not silently dropped. (3) **My Support Tickets** — real `/support/tickets` (list) and `/support/tickets/[id]` (detail) for a signed-in user's own `SupportRequest` rows, both strictly filtered/checked against `requesterUserId === session.user.id` (a real ownership boundary, independently verified). Added a "My tickets" link to the existing `/support` page (purely additive — existing `SupportPageClient` wiring untouched). No schema changes. All three independently typechecked clean (only pre-existing sandbox-wide noise) and grepped clean of mockup placeholder values ("Neon City", "Alex Rivera", etc.). | POST /api/stripe/connect/onboard (Payout Settings), existing SupportRequest/ArtistMediaAsset/MediaListen queries | ✅ Done (code) |
| 227 | (no `.dc.html` — organizer-initiated action, not a new design template) | **Event Cancellation Flow** — real organizer-facing cancellation at `/shows/[slug]/cancel`, distinct from the admin content-moderation cancel path. Gated on `isOrganizer` (venue owner OR headliner owner OR show creator). Only allows cancelling `DRAFT`/`SCHEDULED` shows. `POST /api/shows/[showId]/cancel` walks every `CAPTURED`/`RESERVED` `TicketOrder`: skips (and reports as skipped, not silently dropped) any order with an already-`SCANNED` ticket; for `CAPTURED` orders, refunds via a real `refundTicketPaymentIntent()` Stripe call before voiding the order in the DB (Stripe-first, same ordering as the existing self-serve per-ticket refund route); for `RESERVED` orders, cancels the payment intent and voids the order. Per-order failures are caught individually (`ordersFailed`) rather than aborting the whole batch. Notifies every refunded buyer with an account. Sets `Show.status = 'CANCELED'`, plus new `Show.cancellationReason`/`canceledAt` fields (migration `20260719110000_add_show_cancellation_fields`, applied live). The results screen (`EventCancellationFlow.tsx`) shows the **actual returned counts** (refunded / already-scanned-so-skipped / failed) rather than a blanket "everyone's refunded" message regardless of what really happened. Added a "Cancel event →" link on `/shows/[slug]/page.tsx`'s existing owner-only action row — gated on `isShowOwner` (creator only), narrower than the API's own `isOrganizer` check; a known, accepted small UX gap (venue/headliner owners who aren't the creator can still reach the flow directly by URL and the API itself enforces the real permission). | POST /api/shows/[showId]/cancel | ✅ Done (code + migration applied live) |
| 226 | LineupSplit.dc.html (new `templates/` tree) | **Lineup & Split Agreement — real multi-act payout splits, per explicit product decision ("only applies when multiple acts are booked for a single event; splits are proposed by venue and accepted or rejected by artists").** This was the one piece of the whole design-sync pass deliberately held back for a human decision, since it touches the payout-split logic directly — built only after that decision landed. New `ShowLineupSlot` model (migration `20260719100000_add_show_lineup_slot`, applied to the live DB via the Supabase MCP tool) — a show with zero rows here is completely unaffected, same single-headliner payout as always. **Core payout change** (`src/lib/ticket-order-state.ts`'s `buildPayableEntries`): when lineup slots exist, `order.artistPayoutCents` is split across ACCEPTED slots proportionally by `splitPercent` (siblings sum to `Show.artistPayoutPercent`), with the last slot absorbing the rounding remainder so the split always sums to the exact captured cent amount — no leakage, no double-pay. **Booking-lock gating reuses an existing mechanism rather than adding a new one**: `/shows/[slug]/page.tsx` and the public shows listing already hide `DRAFT` shows, so a lineup-pending show simply stays `DRAFT` until every named act accepts; `PATCH /api/shows/[showId]/lineup/respond` flips it straight to `SCHEDULED` in the same request as the deciding accept — no separate "publish" step to forget. **API**: `POST`/`GET /api/shows/[showId]/lineup` (venue proposes/revises — any submission resets every slot to `PENDING` since a changed split invalidates prior approvals; validates splits sum to the show's `artistPayoutPercent` and exactly one headliner), `PATCH .../lineup/respond` (an artist accepts/declines their own slot; notifies the venue via the existing `notifyUser()` on decline or on lock). **UI**: real `/shows/[slug]/lineup` page — split-bar visualization, per-act status cards, accept/decline for the viewer's own pending slot (`LineupSplitResponder.tsx`), and a lineup composer for the venue owner (`VenueLineupComposer.tsx`, resolves typed profile slugs to real IDs via the existing `/api/search`). Relinked the artist/venue dashboards' upcoming-show rows to this page for `DRAFT` shows instead of the public show page. **Known scope boundary, not silently missing:** the DJ dashboard's own upcoming-shows list only queries shows that DJ promotes/hosts, not shows where they're booked as a lineup act on someone else's venue-booked show — a DJ lineup member still gets the real in-app+push notification linking straight to `/shows/[slug]/lineup`, they just won't also see it surfaced on their dashboard; expanding that query was left for a follow-up rather than folded in here. The venue composer's profile lookup is by exact slug (no autocomplete) — a real, working v1, not a polished picker. Independently typechecked every touched/new file (only the same pre-existing sandbox-wide noise) and re-read the payout-split math by hand for correctness. | POST/GET /api/shows/[showId]/lineup, PATCH /api/shows/[showId]/lineup/respond | ✅ Done (code + migration applied live) |
| 225 | ArtistOnboarding.dc.html, DJOnboarding.dc.html, VenueOnboarding.dc.html (new `templates/` tree) | **Real multi-step setup wizards, done autonomously while the user was away from their PC** (explicit ask: "keep going"). Distinct from `/welcome`'s existing static role-aware "first move" cards — these actually persist data at every real step, since the Profile row for each role already exists from registration (`src/app/api/register/route.ts`'s `db.profile.create`). Built via a 3-agent parallel workflow + an independent verify pass: `src/app/artists/[slug]/onboarding` + `ArtistOnboardingWizard.tsx` (name/genre → optional `/events/new` → real Stripe Connect onboarding via `POST /api/stripe/connect/onboard`), `src/app/promoters/[slug]/onboarding` + `DJOnboardingWizard.tsx` (name/city → genre/link → radio-schedule preference → real `POST /api/verify` submission), `src/app/venues/[slug]/onboarding` + `VenueOnboardingWizard.tsx` (name/city → capacity/room type → booking-preferences info screen → real `POST /api/verify` submission). Added `Profile.capacity`/`roomType` (migration `20260719090000_add_venue_capacity_room_type`, **applied to the live DB same session** once DB access was authorized) for the Venue wizard's room-details step, wired into the existing PATCH `/api/profile-editor`. The DJ wizard's "radio schedule" step (Weekly/Occasional) is the one deliberate no-op in the whole batch — no schema field backs it and nothing else in the app reads it, documented inline rather than faked as persisted. Dropped the Venue wizard's "insurance & compliance checklist" link since `VenueCompliance.dc.html` has no live route in this codebase. Fan/Promoter onboarding templates were not built — `/welcome` already covers those roles adequately without a multi-step wizard, and building one would have required new User-level schema (city/genre capture with nowhere to persist) for comparatively low value. Independently re-verified (not just the agents' self-report): confirmed `PATCH /api/profile/genre` and all linked routes are real, grepped for leftover mockup content (clean — only expected input placeholders like "e.g. Nyla Park"), confirmed the compliance link and AI Page Creator link (redirected to the real `/pages?tab=creator`, since no dedicated AI Page Studio route exists) are correct, and independently typechecked all 6 files (only the same pre-existing sandbox-wide module-resolution noise, cross-checked against unrelated pre-existing files to confirm it's not a real regression). | PATCH /api/profile-editor (capacity/roomType), PATCH /api/profile/genre, POST /api/stripe/connect/onboard, POST /api/verify | ✅ Done (code + migration applied live) |
| 224 | BookingInbox.dc.html, SponsorDashboard.dc.html (new `templates/` tree) | **Two independent, unattended-safe pieces of net-new work** (no schema/product decisions needed, done while checking in wasn't required). (1) **Booking Inbox** — real dedicated `/venues/[slug]/booking-inbox` page (owner-only), a fuller Pending/Accepted/Declined-tabbed view than the existing pending-only `BookingRequestInbox.tsx` embedded on the venue's own profile page. Same real `GET`/`PATCH /api/booking-requests` (accept/decline already fully real, unchanged) — new `src/components/VenueBookingInboxTabs.tsx` adds the tabs and a "View profile" link, which required extending the GET route's select to include the requester's own ARTIST/DJ profile (slug/type/genres/city) rather than exposing their email (the mockup's "Email" quick action was dropped — no reason to surface another user's raw email address without an explicit product decision to do so). Relinked the venue dashboard's two "Booking Inbox"/"Review booking requests" quick actions from the `/me/booking` fallback (row 221) to this new route, and added a Pages-toolkit entry. (2) **Sponsor Dashboard reskin** — confirmed again (see row 221's original finding) that Sponsor = the existing `/advertise/dashboard` advertiser flow, not a new role. Added a real stat-card row (Spend, Impressions, Effective CPM, Active Campaigns + budget remaining) computed from existing `Ad.spentCents`/`budgetCents`/`impressions` — no fabrication, no schema change. Found a real limitation while building this: there is **no actual Stripe charge flow for ad spend anywhere in the codebase** — `budgetCents` is a pre-allocated notional number from the campaign quote, `spentCents` increments deterministically per impression, but no invoice/payment is ever actually collected from an advertiser. Deliberately did not build the mockup's "Billing & invoices" or "Verification status" quick actions since neither has any real backing (no invoice model, no advertiser identity-verification flow) — flagged here rather than building fake UI for either. Both typechecked clean (only pre-existing sandbox noise) and grepped clean of mockup placeholder numbers. | GET /api/booking-requests (now includes requester's own performer profile) | ✅ Done (code) |

| 75 | lib/shell.css + lib/micro.css | **CRITICAL FIX:** the site-wide page-entrance animation (`ihype-rise`, applied to `.page`/`#root`/`.wrap`/etc. on nearly every page) and the new Phase-2 `ihypeFadeSlide` both animated `opacity: 0 → 1`. Verifier caught Artist.dc.html rendering **completely invisible** — `#root` opacity stuck at 0 indefinitely even though React had rendered all content correctly underneath. Root cause: gating real content's visibility on an animation resolving is unsafe — if the animation stalls/restarts/never fires for any reason (timer throttling, backgrounded tab, etc.), the whole page can go permanently blank. Fixed by removing `opacity` from both keyframes, keeping only the `translateY` slide — worst case now is a harmless few-px static offset, never invisible content. This pattern (visible end-state as the base, motion as pure enhancement) now applies everywhere both animations are used. | — | ✅ Done |

| 94 | robots.txt (NEW), sitemap.xml (NEW), Index.dc.html, + noindex meta on 38 .dc.html files | **SEO funnels to the site only — total aggregation, zero per-user indexing.** Only 5 pages indexable: Index, Legal, Charter, Support, Advertise (all aggregate/institutional, no user data). Every other page (Artist/Venue/DJ/FanProfile, Show, Events, Radio, Search, Pages, Settings, Payout, AdminDash, Auth, all account surfaces) got `noindex, nofollow` + canonical back to homepage. `robots.txt` disallows all user-content route prefixes (`/artists/`, `/venues/`, `/fans/`, `/shows/`, `/events`, `/radio`, `/me/`, `/admin`, etc.) so no individual artist/DJ/venue page, ticket, or show can surface in search — discovery only happens inside the product. `sitemap.xml` lists only the 5 indexable pages. Added description/OG/Twitter-card meta to Index.dc.html (had none). | Backend must serve robots.txt/sitemap.xml at domain root and honor per-route noindex when server-rendered | 🟡 Policy has diverged from this spec, undocumented (audit, 2026-07-13) — the live `robots.ts`/`sitemap.ts` do the **opposite** of what this row describes: they now allow and actively index `/artists`, `/shows`, `/venues` (individual pages enumerated in the sitemap) rather than blocking all user-content routes. This may well be an intentional later SEO/growth pivot (organic discovery is valuable for a marketplace like this), but no later DESIGN_SYNC row documents the change — flagging so a future session doesn't assume `noindex` is still the policy. **Decision (2026-07-14, "do all above"):** keeping the current indexed behavior rather than reverting to the original spec. Reasoning: reverting is the harder-to-undo action here (deindexing live pages and regaining search ranking later takes real time, even if reverted again), whereas the current state has been live in production with no evidence of actual harm or a user complaint — just missing documentation. Since there's no clear business-owner directive either way and this is fundamentally a growth-vs-privacy tradeoff rather than a bug, chose the reversible-by-doing-nothing option: formalizing the status quo as the deliberate policy instead of guessing at a reversal. If the original privacy-first intent still matters, this is a one-line `robots.ts` change to revisit. |

| 178 | src/lib/MobileShellContext.tsx, scripts/lighthouse-budget.mjs (NEW), .github/workflows/ci.yml, package.json, .gitignore | **"What would make this app top tier?" Confirmed via Lighthouse's own `layout-shifts` audit: the shifted node was `body > div.site-shell` (near the whole viewport) with a CLS score of 0.81 on `/shows` — not noise, reproduced identically across runs. Fixed by swapping the `useState`+`useEffect` pair for `useSyncExternalStore` (React's blessed mechanism for exactly this — subscribing to a browser API like `matchMedia` and resolving to the true client value synchronously during hydration, before the browser ever paints the stale value), with `getServerSnapshot` unchanged at `false` so SSR output is untouched. **Verified the fix directly**: `/shows` and `/discover` CLS dropped from 0.813/0.016 to 0.000 and their Lighthouse performance scores jumped from 0.59-0.70 to 0.92-0.93, measured before/after against the same production build and real Postgres. Budgets themselves were calibrated empirically rather than guessed — every page in this test harness clusters around a ~3200-3450ms LCP floor regardless of actual weight (this sandbox's `next start` + shared CPU, not the app), so thresholds sit with real headroom above that observed floor per page; `/`'s CLS budget is deliberately 0.15 (one notch under "good") rather than 0.1 like the others, since its CLS is genuinely bimodal (0.000 on most runs, ~0.134 on some) even across a 5-run median — a timing-dependent shift somewhere in that long marketing page's early render that's flagged as a tracked follow-up rather than guess-fixed without the design context for what's actually on it. **Verified:** tsc clean, vitest 206/206, guard:design clean, full mobile-shell e2e suite green (8 passed/1 env-skip, confirming the useSyncExternalStore swap didn't disturb any existing shell interaction), and the Lighthouse budget script itself passing end-to-end against a real production build + real Postgres both before wiring into CI. | — | ✅ Done (code), CI wiring proves itself on this PR's own run |
| 179 | .github/workflows/ci.yml, scripts/lighthouse-budget.mjs, scripts/workerd-smoke.mjs, src/app/globals.css | **CI failure follow-up to row 178, same day.** PR #474's own CI run failed: the Lighthouse budget step booted `npm run build && next start` (plain Node), and every DB-backed page hung retrying Prisma queries against the production `@prisma/client/wasm` import for 25s per attempt before throwing "loaded wasm module was unexpectedly undefined" — the exact same workerd-only limitation documented in row 176/the Prisma regression-guard test, just re-discovered the hard way by building a CI step that violated it. Root-caused via Lighthouse's `layout-shifts` audit: `MobileAppShell` is `next/dynamic(..., {ssr:false})`, deliberately split into its own chunk so desktop never pays for it — so even with `shell.active` resolving synchronously (row 178's fix), `RouteShellSlot` hides the real routed content immediately while the shell's *separate, lazy* chunk is still downloading. During that gap `<main>` (a real, non-fixed, normal-document-flow element) measures zero height, and since the eventual shell replacement is `position:fixed` (contributes no flow height), nothing reserves that space — `<SiteFooter/>`, sitting right after `<main>` in the actual document, jumps upward to fill it, regardless of what's visually painted on top. A synchronous-placeholder approach was tried first (render a `.mas-root.is-active`-classed div immediately, no new bundle weight) and empirically did NOT fix it — confirmed via 5 repeated measurements still showing 0.37-0.85 CLS — because a `position:fixed` placeholder has the identical flow-space problem as the real shell. The fix that actually worked, verified via 15+ repeated measurements all landing at exactly CLS 0.000: `#main-content { min-height: 100dvh; }` scoped to the existing `max-width:768px` mobile breakpoint — keeps the document's own layout height stable across the swap regardless of shell-chunk load timing, which a fixed-position overlay structurally cannot do. Also fixed a related crash: Lighthouse can return a *successful* result with a `null` performance score (a partial-computation failure adjacent to the known `NO_LCP` flake) instead of throwing, which was silently corrupting the median() calculation — now throws explicitly so the existing retry logic catches it. **Budgets recalibrated a second time**, now against genuine, repeated workerd/wrangler-dev measurements (not `next start`'s, which don't transfer — workerd dev consistently runs slower: up to ~4400-5100ms LCP and 700-1000ms+ TBT even on the lightest pages, vs. next start's ~3200-3450ms floor) — all 5 pages pass reliably across multiple consecutive full runs. **Verified:** tsc clean, vitest 206/206, guard:design clean, full mobile-shell e2e green (8/1-skip), and the complete `workerd-smoke.mjs` (functional checks + Lighthouse budget, exactly as CI invokes it) run end-to-end against a real wrangler dev instance and real Postgres — exit 0, every check PASS. | — | ✅ Done (code), CI wiring proves itself on this PR's own (re-)run |

Why the subpath matters: with `engineType = "client"`, the generated `.prisma/client` package routes its main entry through a conditional `#main-entry-point` imports map that lists the `node` condition BEFORE `workerd`; OpenNext's esbuild bundles with BOTH conditions active (platform=node adds `node`, plus its explicit `["workerd"]`), so the `node` branch wins and the native/library engine gets selected — producing exactly row 171's live "Wasm code generation disallowed" and row 172/175's "could not locate the Query Engine" depending on engineType. | 173 | prisma/schema.prisma | **Row 172's `prisma-client` provider switch deployed and genuinely fixed the WASM issue — confirmed live, the error changed** from "Wasm code generation disallowed by embedder" to a completely different message: `Invalid \`prisma.magicLinkToken.findUnique()\` invocation: Prisma Client could not locate the Query Engine for runtime ...` (truncated by the route's own 120-char error-detail limit). Root cause: `provider = "prisma-client"` alone (without an explicit `engineType`) apparently doesn't default to the pure-JS, driver-adapter-only "client" engine the way row 172 assumed from the official docs example — it falls back to expecting a native query-engine binary for some runtime, which doesn't exist in (and can't run in) Cloudflare's Workers sandbox. Confirmed via the generated output itself: without `engineType`, `src/generated/prisma` included a bundled `libquery_engine-debian-openssl-3.0.x.so.node` native binary; adding `engineType = "client"` back (this time paired with the *correct* `provider = "prisma-client"`, unlike the row-171 attempt that paired it with the wrong legacy provider and triggered the original WASM bug) removes that binary from the generated output entirely — confirmed via direct `find`, zero `.wasm`/`.so.node` files anywhere in `src/generated/prisma`. This is the missing half of row 172's fix: `provider` selects the code-generation templates, `engineType` independently selects the actual runtime engine strategy — both needed to be right together, and only one specific combination (new provider + `engineType: "client"`) produces a truly binary-and-WASM-free client suitable for Workers. **Local testing cannot distinguish this class of bug at all** — Node.js resolves/loads whatever native binary or WASM asset it needs from the real filesystem without restriction, so every local repro this session (`next dev`, `next build`, full `cf:build`) "worked" regardless of which engine configuration was actually set; only `workerd`'s sandbox, which this sandbox cannot run, can surface a missing-engine-binary or disallowed-WASM-compilation error. Verified via `tsc --noEmit` (clean), `vitest run` (204 passed, unchanged), `next build --webpack` and `npm run cf:build` (both clean), and direct inspection of the OpenNext-bundled output confirming the native binary is gone (the WASM fallback cache noise identified and ruled out in row 172 is still present and still believed inert, unchanged from that analysis). **Not provable locally, same caveat as every step of this investigation**: whether `engineType = "client"` fully resolves the live error can only be confirmed by testing production directly once deployed. | — | ✅ Done (code), pending user confirmation |

| 167 | src/app/api/auth/magic-link/route.ts | **"Cannot send magic link to admin@ihype.org or sign up with ihypetest7@gmail.com" (2026-07-07, screenshot attached — /login showing "Request failed." after tapping "Send sign-in link").** Traced the generic "Request failed." string to `api-client.ts`'s `apiFetch()`: it's the hardcoded fallback used only when a non-2xx response's body isn't valid JSON with a string `error` field — meaning the actual failure wasn't a normal validation error (those return real messages like "Email is required."), it was an unhandled exception producing a non-JSON response. Found the real gap: `/api/auth/magic-link/route.ts` had **no top-level try/catch** around its `consumeRateLimit`/`db.user.findUnique`/`db.magicLinkToken.create` calls, unlike `/api/register/route.ts`'s full-function try/catch that already turns every failure into a proper `{error: string}` JSON response. In production the DB is reached through Cloudflare Hyperdrive (confirmed in `src/lib/db.ts`) — a pooled proxy where a transient connection reset/cold-start is a real, expected occurrence class, and with no handler in this route such a blip would throw straight through the handler, most likely surfacing as a non-JSON error response at the edge instead of Next's structured JSON error. This single gap explains **both** halves of the report as one root cause, not two: `AuthLogin.tsx`'s login-screen magic-link send calls this route directly, and `AuthRegister.tsx`'s signup flow (`sendSignupMagicLink()`) calls this exact same endpoint as its second step, right after account creation succeeds — so a blip here breaks signup too, even though `/api/register` itself was never at fault. Fixed by wrapping the full handler body in the same try/catch-then-JSON-500 pattern already used by `/api/register`, with a `log.error('[magic-link]', ...)` call matching that route's logging convention. Verified locally against a real Postgres instance (not the production Hyperdrive path, which isn't reachable from this sandbox): confirmed the fixed route still returns the correct `{ok:true}`/`{error:'Email is required.'}`/`{error:'Invalid request.'}` responses for the normal success/validation paths (no regression), and confirmed via code inspection that any exception thrown between those checks now reliably returns `{error:'Something went wrong. Please try again.'}` (500) instead of an unhandled crash. Also verified via `tsc --noEmit`, `vitest run` (204 passed, unchanged), `next build --webpack` (clean, all routes compile). **Not verified against the actual Hyperdrive/production connection-reset scenario** — this sandbox has no route to the real Cloudflare Hyperdrive binding to reproduce the transient blip directly; the fix is a defensive-but-directly-motivated correctness gap (matching the already-established pattern in the sibling `/api/register` route) rather than a reproduced-and-confirmed root cause. | POST /api/auth/magic-link (existing) | ✅ Done (code) |

| 164 | TurnstileWidget.tsx, AuthRegister.tsx | **"Error when trying to setup test artist account" — "Bot check failed. Please try again." on registration (2026-07-07, screenshot attached).** Also chased down (but could not reproduce) a separate prior report of "Known login says passkey verification failed" on `/login` — built a full local repro rig for that first (real local Postgres in this sandbox, `prisma db push` against it, then drove the actual `/register`→`/login` pages in a real browser via Chrome DevTools' WebAuthn virtual-authenticator API — not a mock, an actual credential-create/get ceremony against the live Prisma 7 + `@prisma/adapter-pg` stack this session migrated to). Ruled out, with direct evidence: Prisma 7's `Bytes`-field change (`Buffer`→`Uint8Array`) corrupting stored public keys (wrote a byte-for-byte round-trip test through the real client — bytes matched exactly); a full register→sign-out→sign-in-with-passkey cycle (succeeded); three repeated sign-out/sign-in rounds to catch counter/replay-tracking bugs the way real synced Apple/Google passkeys — which freeze `signCount` at 0 — are known to break naive implementations (all three succeeded, `@simplewebauthn/server`'s counter check already handles the frozen-zero case correctly). Could not reproduce that one and reported back asking for repro details instead of shipping a speculative fix. **This session's next message turned out to be the real, adjacent bug**, caught while setting up a test account the same way: registration failing bot-check is a completely different code path (`AuthRegister.tsx`'s Turnstile widget, checked before any passkey code runs) from the login report, and this one *was* reproducible by code review alone. Root cause: Cloudflare Turnstile tokens are single-use — `TurnstileWidget.tsx` fetched one token on mount and held it in React state indefinitely, with `window.turnstile.reset()` (present on the component's own TypeScript declaration) never called anywhere in the codebase. Any failed `/api/register` submission — a genuine bot-check failure, or *any other* validation error like a duplicate email — consumes that token at Cloudflare's end regardless of why our own logic rejected it, so every retry after the very first failure was guaranteed to fail the same bot check again, forever, with no recovery short of a full page reload. Exactly matches "Bot check failed. Please try again" being shown to someone who evidently *did* try again. Fixed by exposing a `reset()` method off `TurnstileWidget` (`forwardRef`/`useImperativeHandle`, calling the already-declared-but-unused `window.turnstile.reset(widgetId)`) and calling it — along with clearing the stale token from state — in `AuthRegister.tsx`'s catch block, but only on the branch where the account wasn't actually created yet (`!accountCreated`); the passkey-ceremony-retry branch is untouched since `createAccountOnce()` already short-circuits past `/api/register` once an account exists, so Turnstile staleness never applies there. `TurnstileWidget` has exactly one call site (`AuthRegister.tsx`), confirmed by grep, so no other flow needed updating. **Verified this one live and completely**, unlike most fixes this session: since this sandbox has no route to Cloudflare's real Turnstile challenge, injected a faithful mock of `window.turnstile` (`render`/`reset`/callback semantics matching the real API) into a real browser session driving the real `/register` UI, plus a routed `/api/register` that fails the first submission and only accepts the second if it carries a *different* token than the first. Confirmed end-to-end: attempt 1 fails and shows the error, `turnstile.reset()` fires automatically, the mock delivers a fresh token, attempt 2 succeeds using that new token with zero user action beyond clicking "try again." Also verified via `tsc --noEmit`, `vitest run` (204 passed, unchanged), `next build --webpack` (clean), `e2e/mobile-shell.spec.ts` (7 passed, 1 appropriately skipped). | — | ✅ Done (code) |
| 163 | src/app/page.tsx | **"Index still doesn't fit" (2026-07-07, screenshot attached) — mobile horizontal overflow on the homepage hero.** This one was actually reproducible live in this sandbox, unlike the DB-backed pages this session keeps flagging as code-review-only: `/`'s stat counts are already wrapped in `.catch(() => 0)`, so pointing the dev server at an unreachable placeholder `DATABASE_URL` renders the real page with `0` stats instead of crashing — used Playwright at a 390px viewport to measure `document.documentElement.scrollWidth` directly rather than guess from the screenshot. Root cause: the hero's headline is hard-broken into three `<br/>`-separated lines ("Independent" / "music built" / "for the scene.") with no `overflow-wrap`, and "Independent" is a single unbreakable word. On a narrow phone the CSS Grid item wrapping the hero copy (`gridTemplateColumns: '1fr auto'`, a leftover 2-column layout with only one column ever populated) has the browser-default `min-width: auto`, which resolves to that word's full min-content width — confirmed by instrumenting the live DOM: the grid's `1fr` track was computing to `479.86px` inside a `350px` container, a classic "CSS Grid blowout." Fixing only the grid sizing (`min-width: 0` on the item) shrank the track but the still-unbreakable word simply rendered past its new, narrower box instead (`overflow: visible` is the default) — confirmed empirically that `min-width` alone left `scrollWidth` unchanged at `500` vs a `390` viewport. Only combining `min-width: 0` on the grid item *and* `overflow-wrap: break-word` on `.idx-hero-h1` actually closed the gap — reverified live, `scrollWidth` dropped to exactly `390`, matching `clientWidth`. Tried `hyphens: auto` first for a cleaner mid-word break than a raw character split, but it didn't visibly hyphenate in this sandbox's headless Chromium (no hyphenation dictionary installed) so it was dropped rather than ship something unverifiable — the plain `break-word` result ("Independe-/nt") is blunter than a real hyphen but has zero overflow and matches standard mobile-web fallback behavior for a word that can't fit at any reasonable hero font size (even the mobile clamp's floor, 2.5rem, isn't small enough to fit "Independent" in the ~350px content width without breaking it). Full-page rescan after the fix confirmed the only remaining elements whose raw geometry exceeds the viewport (`.idx-role-card`, `.site-background-orb-a/b`) are correctly contained by their own intentional `overflow-x:auto` carousel and `overflow:hidden` background wrapper respectively — not real page-level overflow, and out of scope. Verified via `tsc --noEmit`, `vitest run` (204 passed, unchanged), `next build --webpack` (clean), `e2e/mobile-shell.spec.ts` (7 passed, 1 appropriately skipped), **and**, unusually for this session, a real rendered-in-browser confirmation at 390×844 showing `scrollWidth === clientWidth` before shipping — not code-review-only. | — | ✅ Done (code) |

Even once mounted, its own submit handlers pointed searches at `/home?q=...` (which drops the query param entirely once resolved through `/home`'s existing `redirect('/listen')`) instead of `/search?q=...`, so global search was doubly broken: unreachable, and pointed at the wrong destination even if reached. Fixed both: mounted `<SearchBar />` in `layout.tsx`'s header (between the nav tabs and the auth/user-menu group); changed the desktop form's `action` and the mobile overlay's `router.push` target from `/home` to `/search`; gated the component behind `useSession()` (mirrors `SiteNavTabs.tsx`'s existing logged-out-hides pattern from row 150, since search is an app feature, not marketing chrome). Each module's own inline per-tab search (`onSearchTap` in Listen/Events/Pages, hitting `/api/search` directly) is unaffected and was not touched — it's a separate, already-working UX for searching without leaving a module; the header `SearchBar` is the sitewide "search from anywhere" entry point that `/search`'s dedicated results page was actually built for. **Remaining redirect entries reviewed and left alone** (destinations are real specific pages, or grep confirmed no live in-app references and the routes were never real to begin with): the `www→apex` rule, all legacy `/ihype-*.html` static aliases, `/auth→/login`, the four `/admin/*` consolidation redirects, `/listeners/:slug→/fans/:slug`, `/governance`/`/investor`/`/trust`/`/promise`/`/integrity`→`/about`, and the `/home`-catch-all group (`/trending`, `/leaderboard`, `/playlists/curated`, `/workbench*`, `/artists`, `/fans`, `/promoters`, `/venues`, `/playlists`, `/collab`, `/customizer`, `/show-creator`, `/media`, `/hype`, `/launch-readiness`, `/dashboard`, `/listeners`, `/settings/notifications`, `/settings/data`) — none of these have a matching real, current, file-backed page at that exact path the way `/radio`/`/discover`/`/settings`/`/search`/`/beta` did. Verified via `tsc --noEmit`, `vitest run` (194 passed, unchanged), `next build --webpack` (confirms `/search` and `/beta` both compile as real static routes, not redirects). Not visually re-verified live in a real browser — no live DB/session in this sandbox, consistent with this session's other redirect fixes (curl can't validate a corrected redirect chain either, per row 148's note; a real Playwright session would be needed to confirm the header search bar's final rendered position and behavior). | GET /api/search (reused, no change) | ✅ Done (code) |
| 152 | useDragCarousel.ts; e2e/mobile-shell.spec.ts | **Prevent side-to-side swiping inside an open sub-tab (user-requested, 2026-07-07): "When in sub menu (Listen>Charts, for example) prevent side to side swiping (except in Seeds)."** Root cause: `MobileAppShell.tsx`'s cross-section drag-carousel (`useDragCarousel`) attaches its touch listeners to `.mas-track` — the ancestor of every section's content, not just its grid overlay — and was enabled by `!!shell?.active` alone, with no check for whether a sub-tab was actually open. `MobileQuickGrid`'s own grid-overlay swipe is a *separate* mechanism (portaled to `document.body`, so it never reaches `.mas-track` at all) already correctly scoped to grid-mode only — but once a sub-tab like Listen > Charts was open, the grid overlay goes inert and any horizontal drag on the now-visible content fell straight through to `.mas-track`'s always-on listener, silently swiping to the next/previous section instead of whatever the sub-tab itself wanted to do with that gesture. Fixed by checking, at `touchstart`, whether the event's target is inside `.mqg-content:not(.is-hidden)` (every *Home component's own sub-tab content wrapper) and simply not arming the drag if so — grid-mode touches are unaffected (they never reach `.mas-track` in the first place, per above) and Seeds' card-deck gesture needed no special-casing at all: it's built on Pointer Events + `touch-action: none` (`ListenHome.tsx`), an entirely separate event system from the raw Touch events `useDragCarousel` listens for, so it was never fighting this gesture and isn't affected by the fix either way — "except in Seeds" turned out to already be true by construction once sub-tabs generally stopped hijacking the gesture. Added a new, verified-meaningful e2e case ("swiping inside an open sub-tab does not change section") — caught two of my own false-passes before it was solid: an initial version dispatched touch events with no pacing between steps and never reproduced the bug at all, and a second version raced Playwright's `.not.toHaveCSS` assertion against the (buggy) async `setState → history.pushState → re-render` chain, passing on a stale pre-update snapshot instead of actually proving nothing changed. Confirmed the final version genuinely fails against the reverted, pre-fix code (real regression coverage, not a tautology) before restoring the fix. Verified via `tsc --noEmit`, `vitest run` (194 passed, unchanged), `next build --webpack` (clean), and the full `e2e/mobile-shell.spec.ts` suite (7 passed, 1 appropriately skipped, x2 repeat for stability). | — | ✅ Done (code) |

Wired into `notify.ts`'s single `notifyUser()` fan-in point alongside the existing web-push call, so every existing notification trigger (hype milestones, promoter ticket sales, etc.) *and every future one* gets native push for free with zero additional wiring — directly answers "maintain as future updates are added." Safely no-ops (matching the existing VAPID pattern exactly) whenever `FCM_PROJECT_ID`/`FCM_CLIENT_EMAIL`/`FCM_PRIVATE_KEY` aren't set. **Client-side, native-shell-only:** new `NativePushRegistration.tsx`, mounted once in `AppProviders.tsx` — every code path is gated on `Capacitor.isNativePlatform()`, so it's a verified complete no-op on the website/PWA (confirmed: full e2e mobile-shell suite still green with it mounted). On the real native app it requests permission, registers for push, POSTs the real token to `/api/push/register-device`, and handles both a tapped-notification's `link` and a Universal/App Link's URL (via a new `@capacitor/app` `appUrlOpen` listener) by navigating the SPA there — both paths share `resolveInternalPath()` (`deep-link.ts`, pure + unit-tested, 8 cases including a subdomain-suffix spoofing rejection) so a malformed/spoofed URL can never navigate the app off-origin. **Deep-link association files, real but inert until configured:** new `/.well-known/apple-app-site-association` and `/.well-known/assetlinks.json` routes, env-driven (`APPLE_TEAM_ID`, `ANDROID_CERT_SHA256_FINGERPRINTS`) — serve valid, correctly-shaped JSON with empty claims when unset (verified live: both endpoints return well-formed placeholders unset, and correctly populate real values when the env vars are provided), so they're genuinely ready the moment those accounts exist, not fake stand-ins. Root-caused (via temporary instrumentation, since removed) to a real timing race in the *test*, not the product code — `PullToRefresh.tsx` itself is untouched: the test's fixed `waitForTimeout` gesture pacing assumed the refresh's network round-trip would stay slow enough for the assertion to catch the spinner mid-flight, but the directory endpoint's fast (anonymous, no-AI-call) path could resolve so quickly that `refreshing` flips back to `false` before the assertion samples it. Fixed by having the test itself delay the directory response by 500ms via `page.route()` during that one gesture, making the assertion deterministic regardless of real backend latency — verified via 6x repeat-each under 2 parallel workers (previously reproduced the failure ~1/3 to 3/3 runs under the same load) with 0 failures after the fix, plus a full-suite re-run (12 passed, 2 appropriately-skipped). | 137 | ListenHome, EventsHome, PagesHome, MobileQuickGrid, MobileShellContext, MobileAppShell | **Allow swiping between main tabs while viewing a section's grid/home screen (user-requested, 2026-07-06: "Allow swiping between main tabs").** The persistent shell's horizontal drag-carousel (`useDragCarousel`, row 126) already worked, but only once drilled into a tab's content — `MobileQuickGrid`'s grid/home overlay is portaled straight to `document.body` (so it can render above everything with its own z-index), which puts it on a completely separate real-DOM branch from `MobileAppShell`'s `.mas-track`. Native `addEventListener` bubbling follows the actual DOM tree, not the React tree, so `.mas-track`'s touch listeners physically could never see touches that started on the portaled grid overlay — meaning swiping never worked on the exact screen (each section's grid "home") users see most of the time. Fixed by giving `MobileQuickGrid` its own lightweight swipe detection directly on the portaled overlay (axis-locked start/move/end tracking, reusing the existing pure `resolveDragCommit` from `mobileShell.ts` for the same 20%-of-width commit threshold the content-view carousel already uses) via a new optional `onSwipeSection` prop. Rather than duplicate the "which section is next/prev" math in a second place, moved it out of `MobileAppShell`'s local `handleCommit` and into `MobileShellContext` as a new `swipeSection(direction)` method (single source of truth, also now used by `MobileAppShell` itself); each `*Home` component reads it via `useMobileShell()` and passes it straight through to its own `MobileQuickGrid` call. Deliberately not a live drag-follow like the content-view carousel — it's a simple detect-on-release gesture, so on commit `shell.setSection()` changes and the existing `.mas-slot` transform animates smoothly to the new section (same `.32s cubic-bezier` transition already in place), just without the finger-tracking motion. Scoped safely: since the gesture handlers live only on the portaled overlay div itself (not `document`/`window`), it can't accidentally hijack swipes over the bottom nav, an open `NavDrawer`, or any other unrelated on-screen element. Verified via `tsc --noEmit`, `vitest run` (175 passed), `next build --webpack`; not visually re-verified on a real device (no live DB/browser session in this sandbox). | — | ✅ Done (code) |
| 136 | ListenHome, EventsHome, PagesHome | **Mobile UX follow-ups from a "how else can the mobile view be improved?" audit (Claude Code, 2026-07-06) — user replied "Do all" to 3 candidates.** (1) **Pull-to-refresh, actually wired up:** `globals.css` already had an orphaned `.pull-to-refresh-spinner.spinning` keyframe rule with zero component ever referencing it — built the missing `PullToRefresh.tsx` (native-style: arms only when `window.scrollY === 0`, tracks touch delta with resistance, shows/rotates the existing spinner glyph, calls `onRefresh` past a 64px threshold) and wrapped each module's `.mqg-content` in it, wiring `onRefresh` to each component's own mount-time data fetch (extracted into a reusable `refreshAll`/`refreshDirectory`+`refreshTickets` callback instead of an inline one-shot effect). (2) **Cross-section scroll preservation — audited, already correct, no change needed:** `MobileAppShell`'s `.mas-slot` (one per always-mounted Listen/Events/Pages section) is `position:absolute; overflow-y:auto` and never unmounts, so each section's scroll position already survives swiping away and back — confirmed this was a deliberate existing design (see row 121/126), not a gap. (3) **Real gap found instead: in-section tab switches didn't reset scroll.** Neither the tabstrip pills nor the initial grid→tab tap ever reset `.mas-slot`'s (or, off-shell, the window's) scroll position, so scrolling deep into one tab (e.g. Seeds) and switching to another (e.g. Charts) could land mid-scroll or blank instead of at the top. Fixed with a zero-height sentinel div at the top of each `.mqg-content` plus a `scrollIntoView({block:'start'})` effect keyed on `tab` — works for both the shell's `.mas-slot` scroll container and the plain-page/desktop case without needing to know which ancestor is actually scrolling. **Considered and explicitly declined: converting the sitewide `<img>` usage to `next/image`.** Found the real gap (11 files still on raw `<img>`), but investigation showed `avatarImage`/`galleryImage`/`artworkUrl` are free-text fields (`profile-editor`'s `urlText = z.string().trim().max(2048)`, no protocol/host validation) — a user can point their avatar at any arbitrary `https://` URL, and `next/image` hard-errors on any host not in `next.config.js`'s `remotePatterns` (locked to `ihype.org`/`*.ihype.org` on purpose — the same file's own comment warns a `'**'` wildcard "turns `/_next/image` into an open proxy"). Every one of these `<img>` call sites already carries a deliberate `eslint-disable-next-line @next/next/no-img-element`, confirming this was a prior considered choice, not an oversight — converting them now would trade a performance nicety for a real breakage (any profile with a non-ihype.org avatar 500s) or a real open-proxy risk (widening the wildcard). Left as-is; flagging here in case a scoped `next/image`-with-safe-host-fallback wrapper is wanted later. | 123 | MobileQuickGrid | **Mobile quick-grid overscroll-bounce fix (Claude Code, 2026-07-04), user-reported ("Infinite scroll not working. Button isn't fixed in size (I pulled down and the buttons elongated and it looks bad)").** Follow-up to row 122's containing-block fix — that fixed positioning relative to the true viewport, but nothing stopped the page underneath the overlay from still rubber-band bouncing on iOS Safari when the user dragged down from the top: `useSwipeRouteNav`'s touch listeners are `passive: true` and only handle `touchstart`/`touchend` (no `preventDefault`), so they never blocked the native elastic overscroll. That bounce is a known WebKit rendering bug — during the bounce, fixed-position elements can visibly stretch/distort even though their `top`/`bottom` values never change. Fixed by locking scroll on `<html>`/`<body>` (`overflow: hidden; overscroll-behavior: none`) via a `mqg-scroll-lock` class toggled in a `useEffect` while the grid overlay is `active`, plus `overscroll-behavior: none; touch-action: pan-x` directly on `.mqg-overlay` itself. This matches the grid's original design intent (no scrolling at all — an edge-to-edge, screen-filling grid) rather than adding new scroll behavior. Verified via `tsc --noEmit`, `vitest run` (172 passed), and `next build`; not visually re-verified on a real device. | — | ✅ Done (code) |
| 122 | MobileQuickGrid, layout.tsx | **Mobile quick-grid containing-block fix + PWA prompt removal + footer cleanup (Claude Code, 2026-07-04), user-reported ("Squares not right things bottling up right" / "Still not aligned also drop the add to home screen thing - too busy" / "Remove text footer as it exists in mobile menu").** Real bug from row 121's grid, confirmed via two device screenshots (not a caching issue — reproduced identically after a genuine reload): `globals.css`'s `.site-shell > main { animation: page-enter 0.4s ... both; }` leaves a permanent non-`none` `transform` on `<main>` (fill-mode `both` keeps the final keyframe's transform applied after the animation ends), and any non-`none` transform on an ancestor makes it the containing block for `position:fixed` descendants — so `MobileQuickGrid`'s `.mqg-overlay`, rendered inside `<main>{children}</main>`, was never actually pinned to the true viewport, just to `<main>`'s own box, causing the grid rows to compress/overlap with the real footer showing through underneath. Fixed by having `MobileQuickGrid` render via `createPortal` into `document.body` (gated on a `mounted` state for SSR safety) so it escapes `<main>`'s containing block entirely, matching how every other fixed-position element in the app (bottom nav, cookie banner, player dock) already avoids this by living in `layout.tsx` outside `<main>`. | 117 | (audit only, no design change) | **Sitewide security + accessibility audit (Claude Code, 2026-07-04), user-requested ("ensure all accessibility and security requirements are embedded").** Security: found and fixed a real stored-XSS vulnerability — `src/app/shows/[slug]/page.tsx`'s JSON-LD `<script>` tag interpolated `JSON.stringify(jsonLd)` (built from user-controlled show title/description/profile names) straight into `dangerouslySetInnerHTML`, and `JSON.stringify` does not escape `</script>`, so a title containing that sequence could break out and execute arbitrary script for every visitor. Fixed via a new `toSafeJsonLdString()` helper (`src/lib/safe-json-ld.ts`, unit-tested) that escapes the `<` character to its unicode-escaped form before it reaches the DOM. Also closed the one real gap in the existing cookie-consent flow: the CF Insights beacon in `layout.tsx` loaded unconditionally regardless of the user's cookie choice — new `AnalyticsBeacon.tsx` client component gates it on `localStorage` + a `ihype:cookie-consent` event the banner now dispatches, so it never loads until "Accept all" is chosen. Everything else audited came back clean: `next.config.mjs` already ships a comprehensive header set (HSTS, CSP, X-Frame-Options, COOP/CORP, etc.) applied to every route including `/api/*`; all public unauthenticated write endpoints already rate-limited; all three webhook receivers (Stripe ×2, Resend) verify signatures; session cookies are `httpOnly`+`sameSite:lax`+`secure` (adequate CSRF mitigation); no hardcoded secrets in source; `.env*` properly gitignored; `npm audit` clean apart from one low-severity, Windows-only, dev-tooling-only `esbuild` transitive advisory. Accessibility: the root layout rendered page content as a bare `<div>` with no `<main>` landmark — 33 of 85 pages had their own nested `<main>` (which `globals.css`'s `.site-shell > main` selector was already written to expect for the page-enter fade animation, confirming this was the intended structure, just never centralized) and the other 52 had no main landmark at all. Added a single `<main id="main-content">` in `layout.tsx` wrapping `{children}`, converted the 33 pages' inner `<main>` to `<div>` (mechanical, verified 1-in/1-out per file first) so there's exactly one landmark per page, and added a standard skip-to-content link (off-screen until keyboard-focused).
