per-show `artistPayoutPercent`/`venuePayoutPercent` were never hardcoded here, they flow from caller input). **EventCreator wizard** (`src/app/events/new/page.tsx`): hardcoded `venuePayoutPercent: 45, artistPayoutPercent: 45` → `venuePayoutPercent: 20, artistPayoutPercent: 70`; every visual split-bar `flex` value, dollar-multiplier display (`gross * .45` → `gross * .7`/`.2`), and copy string ("45/45/10 split is automatic", "45% artist · 45% venue · 10% promoters") updated to match. **Payout display pages**: `/payout/[id]` fallback defaults (`?? 45` → `?? 70`/`?? 20`) and split-bar flex values; `/me/payouts` doc-comment reference. **Marketing/legal/charter copy** (about, verify, community, settings, register, shows, shows/[slug], me/promote, me/wrapped, legal, charter, api/og, page.tsx homepage tiles, AuthRegister, WalkthroughDeck's `SPLIT` array + copy) — every "45/45/10", "45% artist / 45% venue", and per-role dollar-share line rewritten to 70/20/10. **Seed data** (`prisma/seed.ts`, `prisma/launch-seed.ts`): per-show `venuePayoutPercent`/`artistPayoutPercent` pairs previously summed to 95 (consistent with the old default-promoter-5% remaining-95% math) — since the default promoter share is now 10% (remaining 90%), left as-is they would have failed `validateTicketSplit()` inside `calculateTicketOrderPayouts()` at seed time. Rescaled every pair to sum to 90, preserving the original venue-heavier/artist-heavier variety across sample shows (e.g. 50/45 → 20/70, 55/40 → 25/65, 42/53 → 15/75) rather than flattening every seeded show to an identical split. **Tests** (`ticketing.test.ts`): two assertions that depended on the changed default — `DEFAULT_PROMOTER_AFFILIATE_PERCENT` toBe(5)→toBe(10), `getRemainingPayoutPercent()` toBe(95)→toBe(90) — plus the one `validateTicketSplit` fixture that relied on the implicit default (45/50 summing to the old 95%) rewritten as the new canonical 70/20 example (20/70 summing to the new 90%) and its sibling error-message assertion ('must total 95%'→'must total 90%'). Every other test fixture in `ticketing.test.ts`/`ticket-scan.test.ts`/`show-purchase.test.ts` passes an explicit `promoterPayoutPercent` alongside its venue/artist values, so those sums (already self-consistent, e.g. 45/50/5=100) were unaffected by the default change and were deliberately left alone rather than churned for cosmetic consistency. **i18n** (`public/i18n/{en,es,fr,pt}.js`): confirmed these files have zero import sites anywhere in `src/` (dead/unwired copy, likely a leftover from an earlier prototype) but are still statically served at `/i18n/*.js` and directly answer "what's the split," so updated all four languages' percentage/ratio references for consistency rather than leaving stale public copy; left illustrative "$45 ticket" dollar-amount examples untouched since those are example ticket prices, not derived from the split percentages. tsc clean, vitest 270/270, lint clean (617 files), guard:design clean, production build succeeds. **Not runtime-verified against a live DB** — no live show/ticket data in this sandbox to confirm an actual purchase computes 70/20/10 end-to-end; the unit-tested `calculateTicketOrderPayouts()` math and the seed-time `validateTicketSplit()` pass are the verification available here. | — | ⏳ Pending — code complete, committed locally, blocked on the same git push access issue as row 219 |
| 219 | prisma/migrations/20260714060000_add_ticket_order_refund_fields (NEW), prisma/schema.prisma, src/lib/stripe.ts, src/lib/ticket-order-state.ts, src/app/api/tickets/[serializedId]/refund/route.ts, src/components/TicketCardActions.tsx, src/app/me/payouts/page.tsx (NEW), src/app/payout/[id]/page.tsx, CLAUDE.md | **"Do anything above you can" follow-up (2026-07-14) on the two remaining ticketing/payout items from row 218's audit, while git push access was blocked (repo appears to have moved to a different GitHub org mid-session; committed locally, ready to ship once access is restored).** **(1) Refund is now real.** `POST /api/tickets/[serializedId]/refund` used to only create a `SupportRequest` and leave the order, tickets, and sold capacity completely untouched — the UI copy said "our support team will process your refund," which meant nothing happened automatically at all. Now: for a `CAPTURED` order, calls the new `refundTicketPaymentIntent()` (a real `stripe.refunds.create()`) first — Stripe is the source of truth, DB only updates after Stripe confirms — then the new `refundCapturedTicketOrder()` (`src/lib/ticket-order-state.ts`, mirrors the existing `voidReservedTicketOrder()` pattern) atomically voids the order, voids any unscanned tickets, releases sold capacity back to the show, and voids any still-`PENDING` `AccountsPayableEntry` rows tied to the order so the payout cron (row 218) can never pay out money for a since-refunded order. That last step is safe by construction, not by a runtime check: payouts only ever run for `ENDED` shows, and a refund is only ever allowed more than 48h before a show starts — so a refundable order's payable entries are provably still `PENDING`, never `RELEASED`, at refund time. For a `RESERVED` (authorized-but-never-captured) order, cancels the Stripe authorization instead of refunding — there's no captured charge to refund. Blocks the refund outright if any ticket in the order has already been scanned (already-attended shows shouldn't self-serve refund). New `TicketOrder.refundedAt`/`stripeRefundId` fields for the audit trail, matching the `stripeTransferId` precedent row 218 added to `AccountsPayableEntry`. Updated the two places `TicketCardActions.tsx` told buyers this was routed to a human — it now correctly says the refund is immediate. **(2) New `/me/payouts` page.** Real payout history for the signed-in user's own profiles (venue/artist/promoter) — every `AccountsPayableEntry` that actually moved money via row 218's `triggerShowPayouts()`, split into Received (`RELEASED`, with the real paid date) and Pending. Distinct from the pre-existing `/payout/[id]`, which shows a computed 45/45/10 projection for one specific show a user created, regardless of whether it's actually been paid out — that page now links to `/me/payouts` for the full history. **Explicitly not done, flagged instead:** tax remittance (`TAX_LOCAL`/`STATE`/`COUNTRY`/`INTERNATIONAL` `AccountsPayableEntry` rows) still has no resolution path and stays `PENDING` forever — that's a real accounting/filing process with a tax jurisdiction, not something a Stripe Connect transfer can do, and building it wasn't in scope here. tsc clean, vitest 270/270 (unchanged — refund/payout-history logic is DB-transaction/query code, same testing posture as the sibling `ticket-order-state.ts` functions it mirrors, no existing test file covers that module either), lint clean (617 files), guard:design clean, production build succeeds (`/me/payouts` compiles). **Not runtime-verified against a live DB or live Stripe** — same standing caveat as row 218, with the same recommendation to run this against Stripe test mode (a captured order → refund → confirm the test-mode refund lands and capacity/tickets/payable-entries all update correctly) before production. **This row's commits are not yet pushed** — mid-session the git push to `colinatwood/ihype` started failing with a persistent 403 (read/fetch still works; the GitHub API independently confirmed the repo now resolves to `iHYPE-org/ihype`, suggesting an org transfer this session's write grant wasn't updated for). Committed locally and ready; push retried repeatedly without success, needs the session's GitHub access re-pointed at the new location. | POST /api/tickets/[serializedId]/refund (now performs a real refund, not just a support ticket) | ⏳ Pending — code complete, committed locally, blocked on git push access |
| 218 | prisma/migrations/20260714030000_add_payable_stripe_transfer_id (NEW), prisma/migrations/20260714040000_add_ad_paused_at (NEW), prisma/migrations/20260714050000_drop_ad_image_url (NEW), prisma/schema.prisma, src/lib/stripe.ts, src/lib/show-payouts.ts, src/app/api/shows/[showId]/tickets/route.ts, src/app/api/tickets/[serializedId]/transfer/route.ts, src/app/api/shows/[showId]/scan/route.ts, src/lib/media-vetting.ts, src/lib/__tests__/media-vetting.test.ts (NEW), src/app/api/artist-media/route.ts, src/lib/ad-vetting.ts, src/app/api/advertise/campaigns/route.ts, src/components/CampaignCancelButton.tsx, src/components/AdminAdsClient.tsx, src/app/advertise/dashboard/page.tsx, CLAUDE.md | **"Do all above" follow-up (2026-07-14) on 4 recommendations — one of which (a fresh ticketing/payout audit) surfaced a severe, previously-undiscovered bug that changed the shape of this whole pass.** Ran the audit as a background research agent first (read-only), which came back with a finding serious enough to stop and ask the user directly before touching payment code: **every ticket sale was routing 100% of the charge to a single party (venue if present, else artist) instead of the charter's 45/45/10 split**, and the "payout" system never actually paid anyone — `AccountsPayableStatus.RELEASED` was never set anywhere in the codebase. Asked explicitly whether to just document this or actually fix live payment code, and separately whether to fix a related ticket-transfer bug the same audit found; user said fix both. **(1) Payout routing — the core fix.** `createTicketPaymentIntent` (`src/lib/stripe.ts`) used to set `transfer_data.destination` to one Connect account with no `amount` sub-field, which per Stripe's own semantics transfers the *entire* captured charge to that single destination — not a split. Real per-order splits were already being computed correctly and stored as `AccountsPayableEntry` rows (`src/lib/ticket-order-state.ts`, unchanged, was already right) — they just never got paid. Switched to the standard "separate charges and transfers" pattern: `createTicketPaymentIntent` no longer sets `transfer_data` at all, so the full charge captures to the platform's own Stripe balance; new `createPayoutTransfer()` issues one real `stripe.transfers.create()` per `AccountsPayableEntry`, idempotent via the entry's own id as the Stripe idempotency key. Completely rewrote `triggerShowPayouts()` (`src/lib/show-payouts.ts`, the `show-payouts` cron job) — the old version didn't touch `AccountsPayableEntry` at all, it independently recomputed a *different, wrong* estimate (hardcoded 5% platform fee / 85% artist share, ignoring venue and promoter entirely) and only ever sent an email promising a payout that never happened. It now processes real `PENDING` entries for `ENDED` shows, actually transfers the money, and only then emails the real recipient. Tax entries (no Connect account, no `profileId`) deliberately stay `PENDING` — remittance is a manual accounting matter, explicitly out of scope rather than silently built. New `AccountsPayableEntry.stripeTransferId` records the real transfer. **(2) Ticket transfer — real double-use fix.** Transferring a ticket used to just email the recipient the *existing* serializedId while leaving the `Ticket` row (status, holder) completely untouched — since every ticket lookup (the public QR page, both scan endpoints) has no ownership check beyond the id itself, the original buyer (who may have already opened, screenshotted, or printed the QR before initiating the transfer) still held a fully valid, scannable copy; whoever scanned first won, a real race. Now reissues every ticket in the order with a brand-new `serializedId` (`createSerializedTicketId()`) inside a `$transaction`, updates `holderName`/`holderEmail` to the recipient, and increments the existing `reassignCount`/`reassignedAt` fields (already used by the separate venue-staff "Venue reassignment" feature on `/tickets/[serializedId]` — reused rather than inventing parallel fields). The old QR now 404s the instant a transfer happens; only the freshly emailed serializedId works. **(3) Also fixed, found during the same audit pass, not explicitly asked but a trivial one-line-shaped fix matching an already-correct sibling:** `/api/shows/[showId]/scan` had a real scan-replay race — `findFirst` then a JS status check then a separate `update`, so two concurrent scans of the same ticket could both pass the check before either write landed. Made it atomic via `updateMany({ where: { id, status: 'VALID' }, ... })` + `result.count`, exactly matching the pattern `/api/tickets/[serializedId]/scan/route.ts` already used correctly — these two endpoints had silently drifted to different levels of correctness despite doing the same job. **(4) Extended real audio-content vetting to track uploads**, the direct analog of the ad-audio vetting built earlier this session (row 215): new `vetTrackAudioContent()` in `src/lib/media-vetting.ts` transcribes vocals/lyrics (Workers AI Whisper, same `runTranscription` used for ads) and checks for a match to a well-known commercial song — augments, not replaces, the existing metadata-only `vetFreeUseSample()` in `POST /api/artist-media`. Instrumental tracks transcribe to nothing and pass through untouched; this is a lyrics/vocal check, not a full acoustic fingerprint match (no such service is configured in this codebase, documented as a known limitation since row 8 of this session). 2 new unit tests confirm the fail-open contract. **(5) Campaign pause/resume**, on top of the cancel action shipped in row 217: new `PAUSED` status + `Ad.pausedAt`; resuming shifts `endsAt` forward by exactly how long the campaign was paused, so a pause never eats into paid-for run length — `PATCH /api/advertise/campaigns` now handles `{action: 'cancel'|'pause'|'resume'}`, `CampaignCancelButton.tsx` renders the right button(s) per status. **(6) Dropped the dead `Ad.imageUrl` field** the same way `AdSubmission` was handled in row 214 — removed from `schema.prisma` (confirmed zero read sites anywhere in `src/`), gated/unapplied drop migration (`prisma/migrations/20260714050000_drop_ad_image_url`) since historical rows from before this session's earlier campaigns-route change may have set it; explicit "DO NOT APPLY BLIND" header, same as the `AdSubmission` migration. tsc clean (cleared stale `.next` type cache after the schema changes), vitest 270/270 (2 new), lint clean (616 files), guard:design clean, production build succeeds. **Not runtime-verified against a live DB or live Stripe** — same sandbox limitation as every prior row, but flagged with extra weight here: the payout fix specifically **has never executed against a real Stripe Connect account or moved real money in this sandbox** — strongly recommend a full Stripe test-mode run (a captured order → `triggerShowPayouts` → confirm three real test-mode transfers land in the right test Connect accounts for the right amounts) before this reaches production, given the severity of what it's replacing. | POST /api/advertise/campaigns (now handles pause/resume actions too), createTicketPaymentIntent (no longer sets transfer_data — behavior change on every ticket purchase), triggerShowPayouts (rewritten — now moves real money instead of emailing an estimate), POST /api/tickets/[serializedId]/transfer (reissues serializedIds), POST /api/shows/[showId]/scan (now atomic) | ✅ Done (code) — payout fix not live-verified, flagged for a real Stripe test-mode run before production |
| 217 | src/lib/ad-campaign-notify.ts (NEW), src/components/CampaignCancelButton.tsx (NEW), src/app/api/advertise/campaigns/route.ts, src/app/api/admin/ads/route.ts, src/app/advertise/dashboard/page.tsx, src/components/AdminAdsClient.tsx, src/lib/ad-vetting.ts | **"Do all above" follow-up (2026-07-14) on 4 recommendations surfaced after row 216 (the SSRF fix).** All 4 shipped; the 5th ("consider a fresh sitewide sweep") ran as an actual check, not just a suggestion — see below. **(1) Self-serve campaign cancel.** New `AdCampaignStatus` value `CANCELLED` (`src/lib/ad-vetting.ts`) — set only by the advertiser's own action, never by vetting. New `PATCH /api/advertise/campaigns` (`{id, action: 'cancel'}`) checks the requester owns the campaign, then sets it `CANCELLED`; no new guard needed elsewhere, since every consumer of `Ad` rows (`resolveAdBreakClips`, the impression route) already filters `status: 'APPROVED'`, so a cancelled campaign stops being selected or credited automatically. New `CampaignCancelButton.tsx` client component on `/advertise/dashboard`. Deliberately shipped as **cancel only, not pause/resume** — a resumable paused state is a materially bigger feature (needs its own status, resume logic, re-validation that budget/dates still make sense) than what was asked ("can't pause or cancel"); cancel covers the actual complaint (no way to stop a runaway campaign) without inventing scope. **(2) Status-change email.** New shared `src/lib/ad-campaign-notify.ts` (`notifyAdvertiser()`, reuses the existing `sendEmailToUser()` — which already skips bounced addresses — rather than a bespoke send) fires on the initial AI vetting result in `POST /api/advertise/campaigns` and on an admin's manual approve/reject in `PATCH /api/admin/ads` (which previously did neither — an advertiser's only way to learn their campaign's fate was to keep checking the dashboard). Fire-and-forget, `.catch()`'d — a failed send never blocks the campaign response. **(3) Removed the permanently-zero Clicks/CTR stats from `/advertise/dashboard`.** Confirmed `Ad.clicks` has genuinely zero incrementing callers anywhere in the codebase — unlike the retired `AdSubmission`/`AdBanner` system, which had a real `/api/ads/[id]/click` redirect (deleted in row 214), a radio audio spot has no click-through UI at all, so the field can only ever read 0. Rather than either building an entirely new click-tracking surface for a format that has no natural click target (what would clicking an audio spot even mean — a "info" button during playback? a companion visual card? neither exists nor was asked for) or leaving a stat tile that lies by omission, removed the Clicks/CTR tiles (both the aggregate row and per-campaign) — impressions and budget-remaining stay, since those are real. `clickUrl` itself is untouched (still collected, still shown as a link on the dashboard — it's real advertiser-provided metadata, just not something a listener can currently click from inside a radio show). **(4) Fresh sitewide SSRF sweep**, prompted directly by row 216's finding: grepped every `await fetch(` call in `src/app/api` for the same "URL comes from user input, unvalidated" shape. Found two others: `page-hero/route.ts` (Unsplash search — host is a hardcoded literal, only a URL-encoded query param is user-controlled, not vulnerable) and `page-builder/import-website/route.ts` (the AI Page Studio's "import from your website" feature, which **does** fetch an arbitrary user-submitted URL by design) — already hardened with a dedicated `validatePublicHttpUrl()` (`src/lib/safe-external-url.ts`) that rejects private/internal ranges and re-validates on every redirect hop, a materially more complete defense than what this row's fix needed (that route has to accept genuinely arbitrary public URLs; the ad-audio fetch only ever needed to accept iHYPE's own storage). No new issue found, but confirms row 216's pattern was the outlier, not a symptom of a wider gap. Also ran `npm audit --omit=dev`: 0 vulnerabilities. tsc clean, vitest 268/268 (unchanged — no new pure-logic module warranted new tests; `ad-campaign-notify.ts` is a thin email-template wrapper, same posture as its siblings), lint clean (615 files), guard:design clean, production build succeeds. **Not runtime-verified against a live DB or live email delivery** — same sandbox limitation as every prior row. | PATCH /api/advertise/campaigns (NEW — self-serve cancel), PATCH /api/admin/ads (now emails the advertiser) | ✅ Done (code) |
| 216 | src/lib/object-storage.ts, src/app/api/advertise/campaigns/route.ts, src/lib/__tests__/object-storage.test.ts (NEW) | **CodeQL security finding on merged PR #516 (2026-07-14, `github-advanced-security[bot]`) — Server-Side Request Forgery, fixed same-day.** Row 215's audio-content vetting fetched `audioUrl` — a client-submitted string — directly server-side (`fetch(audioUrl)` in `POST /api/advertise/campaigns`) with no validation that it actually pointed at iHYPE's own storage. A malicious client could have set `audioUrl` to an internal service address (e.g. a cloud metadata endpoint) and had the server fetch it on their behalf. **By the time CodeQL's alert and CI failure arrived, PR #516 had already merged** — this shipped to `main` before the scan finished, so the fix here is a same-day follow-up landing directly on `main`, not a review-comment fix on the original PR. New `isTrustedStorageUrl()` in `src/lib/object-storage.ts` (the module that already owns every `storeMediaFile()`-generated URL shape — R2 public base, default R2 endpoint, or an inline `data:` fallback) validates a URL matches one of those before anything is allowed to fetch it back. `campaigns/route.ts` now rejects the campaign outright (400) if `audioUrl` isn't trusted-storage, *before* it's ever used for a fetch — closing both the SSRF (the fetch is now provably safe) and a smaller adjacent issue (a client could otherwise have set an arbitrary external URL as their "ad audio" entirely, not just for the vetting fetch). 8 new unit tests (`object-storage.test.ts`) cover the exact SSRF scenario (arbitrary external URL, cloud-metadata-style internal URL, cross-account R2 URL) alongside the legitimate-URL cases. tsc clean, vitest 268/268 (8 new), lint clean (613 files), guard:design clean, production build succeeds. **Not runtime-verified against a live DB/R2** — same sandbox limitation as every prior row; the URL-matching logic itself is pure and fully covered by the new tests, independent of that limitation. | POST /api/advertise/campaigns (audioUrl now validated, 400 on an untrusted URL) | ✅ Done (code) |

Factored the real-ad-with-placeholder-fallback selection logic out of `GET /api/radio/ad-clips` into a new shared `src/lib/ad-clip-selection.ts` (`resolveAdBreakClips()`), and now call it server-side from both `POST /api/shows` and `PATCH /api/shows/[showId]` whenever `advertising.enabled && clips.length === 0` at save time — so "auto" is actually automatic. `ad-clips/route.ts` now also returns `isMarketplace: boolean` (since it always returns *something*, real-or-placeholder, the client can no longer infer the source from array length alone) — `RadioShowCreator.tsx`'s preview-modal copy reads that flag instead, so the "real campaigns" vs "placeholder catalog" messaging (row 214) stays honest. **(2) Ad audio content itself was never vetted, only the campaign's declared title.** Added `runTranscription()` to `src/lib/ai.ts` (Whisper via Workers AI, `@cf/openai/whisper`, confirmed input/output shape against Cloudflare's docs same as the vision model earlier) and `vetAdAudioContent()` to `src/lib/ad-vetting.ts` — transcribes the spot, then runs the transcript through the same music-industry-policy AI check the text pipeline uses (sampled songs, name-drops, hate speech, off-topic content). Wired into `POST /api/advertise/campaigns`: fetches the just-uploaded `audioUrl`, transcribes, and — fail-open, same as every vetting call in this codebase — downgrades a clean-copy campaign to `PENDING` and raises a `ContentReport` (`targetType: 'ad-audio'`) if the audio itself is flagged even though the title passed. New `enforceRemoval()` case rejects the `Ad` on moderation approval; added to the `/audit` category list and moderation type filter. Also corrected the `AdvertisePage.tsx` "Copyright firewall" copy (row 214 had already fixed the literal "fingerprinted" claim) to say audio is now genuinely transcribed and screened, which it is as of this row. **(3) Wrote the `AdSubmission` drop migration — after asking first.** Row 214 left the model in schema per the never-drop-without-authorization precedent; flagged it back to the user as needing an actual decision rather than indefinite limbo. Asked directly: write the migration now, or leave it flagged. User chose to write it. `prisma/migrations/20260714020000_drop_ad_submission/migration.sql` drops the table, with an explicit **"DESTRUCTIVE — DO NOT APPLY BLIND"** header explaining exactly why (no live DB access from this sandbox means "no code path creates new rows" was verified, but "the table is empty in production" was not — those are different claims) and the concrete steps to confirm before running it. | 201 | src/app/api/auth/signout/route.ts (NEW), src/app/settings/page.tsx | **Fix: "Sign out doesn't work" (user report, 2026-07-12).** `/api/auth/signout` had no dedicated route — it fell through to the `[...nextauth]` catch-all. But sessions here are built by hand (`buildAuthSessionCookie`, not NextAuth's signIn flow), and Auth.js's signout only clears the session on a **CSRF POST** — a GET just renders a confirmation page. So the "Sign out" links (all plain GET navigations) did nothing. Fix: (1) new `src/app/api/auth/signout/route.ts` (GET **and** POST) that expires the exact custom session cookie `getAuthSessionCookieName()` (`__Secure-authjs.session-token` in prod / `authjs.session-token` in dev) plus its chunked `.0`/`.1` variants, with matching options (path `/`, httpOnly, secure, sameSite lax, maxAge 0), then redirects to `/`; a static route takes precedence over the catch-all, which still serves every other `/api/auth/*` path. Session strategy is JWT (stateless), so clearing the cookie fully signs out — no DB session to invalidate, and no `userSecurityVersion` bump (that would sign out every device). (2) `settings/page.tsx` Danger-Zone "Sign out" changed from `<Link>` to a plain `<a>` — a soft client-side nav to an API route won't actually hit it. NavDrawer's signout `<a>` and settings' `window.location.href` were already hard navigations and now resolve correctly. tsc, vitest 254/254, source-policy lint, design guard clean. **Not runtime-verified** (DB/auth blocker) — standard auth-cookie-clearing pattern; recommend a quick signed-in→Sign out click once deployed. | 2026-07-12 |

| 198 | src/components/AuthRegister.tsx | **Fix: iOS mobile Safari couldn't complete passkey registration (alpha-user bug report + screenshot, 2026-07-12: "couldn't register with passkey or magic link from iOS").** Root cause (screenshot showed the passkey step stuck on "Waiting for your device passkey prompt" → "Challenge expired"): the passkey ceremony did `await fetch(register-first)` + `await res.json()` **before** `startRegistration()`. iOS Safari only runs `navigator.credentials.create()` inside the **transient user activation** from a tap; an awaited network fetch between the tap and the ceremony consumes that activation, so the Face ID / passkey sheet silently never appears (Chromium/Android are lenient, which is why it worked elsewhere and wasn't caught). Fix (client-only, all backend wiring — endpoints, bootstrap cookie, server challenge, POST verification — unchanged): **pre-fetch the WebAuthn challenge into a ref** (`preparePasskeyOptions`) as soon as we land on the passkey step, so the "Try passkey again" tap calls `startRegistration()` with the options already in hand — making the ceremony the first awaited call after the gesture, which keeps iOS's activation valid. `registerPasskeyForAccount` gained an optional `prefetched` param (`prefetched ?? await fetchPasskeyOptions()`), `retryPasskey` consumes the warmed options and re-arms a fresh one on failure, and the initial auto-attempt (still inline-fetch, fine on Android/desktop) now warms options in its catch so the retry tap is reliable. Magic-link path was reviewed and is correct (send route + Lax session cookie on the top-level link nav both fine) — the reported magic-link failure is most likely email delivery (infra), not code. **Not device-verified** — the iOS-specific user-activation behavior can't be reproduced in headless Chromium and the app needs DB/auth to run; the fix follows the standard WebAuthn user-activation pattern and is provably no-worse on other platforms (unchanged inline-fetch path). tsc, vitest 250/250, source-policy lint, design guard clean. **Recommend a real iOS Safari signup test once deployed.** | 2026-07-12 |

| 182 | src/app/api/profile-editor/route.ts, src/lib/profile-editor-schema.ts (NEW) | **Fixed "Invalid input" error saving Pages editor changes; investigated "where is the AI page customization engine?" (2026-07-09), both from the same user report.** Root cause of the save error: `PageEditor.tsx`'s `save()` PATCHes its *entire* client-side state back to `/api/profile-editor` on every save, including every field the initial `GET` returned as `null` (nearly all of the ~25 text fields, on any profile that hasn't filled in every field — i.e. almost every real profile). The Zod schema's `text()`/`urlText()` helpers were `z.string().trim().max(n).optional()` — `.optional()` permits `undefined` but explicitly not `null` — so the very first untouched null field failed validation, surfacing Zod v4's generic default message, `"Invalid input"`. Not Theme-tab-specific; it would fire from any tab, for any profile with any empty field. Fixed by adding `.nullable()` to both helpers and updating `emptyToNull()` to pass `null` through instead of only handling `string | undefined`. Extracted the schema out of `route.ts` into `src/lib/profile-editor-schema.ts` (route.ts pulls in `next-auth`/Prisma, which can't resolve under plain vitest — the same `@prisma/client/wasm` local-Node limitation hit elsewhere in this project — so the schema needed to live somewhere dependency-light to be unit-testable) and added a regression test (`profile-editor-schema.test.ts`) asserting a payload shaped like a real mostly-empty-profile GET response parses successfully; confirmed the test fails against the pre-fix schema and passes against the fix. **AI page customization engine: exists in the codebase, but is fully unwired from the UI.** `/api/page-builder/refine` (added 2026-07-03) sends a user's natural-language instruction plus the current theme JSON to Cloudflare Workers AI and returns structured theme-field changes (mood/font/layout/tagline/bio/palette); `/api/page-builder` (GET/PUT) stores a draft page JSON blob per profile (`Profile.pageDraft`/`pageDraftUpdatedAt`), `/api/page-builder/publish` promotes a draft to `pagePublished`/`pagePublishedAt`, and `/api/page-builder/ad-recs` exists alongside it. All four routes are real, working backend code with matching Prisma columns already migrated — but grepping the entire `src/` tree turns up zero client-side references to any of them; no component ever calls `/api/page-builder*`. It's backend-only and unreachable from the live app, same class of issue as the dormant theme-preset system `PageEditor.tsx` itself was built to surface. This needs a `.dc.html` design (per this repo's UI-source-of-truth rule) before a UI can be wired to it — flagging as a real, ready-to-build feature rather than vaporware. tsc clean, vitest 207/207 (206 prior + 1 new), guard:design clean. | — | ✅ Done (code) |

Prisma 7 requires ESM module format, a new generator/output config, driver adapters, a new `prisma.config.ts`, and removes client middleware — and this exact codebase already had a real production outage from a subtle Prisma config regression on Cloudflare Workers (row 177), with a dedicated test now guarding the exact config this upgrade would touch. TypeScript 7 is Microsoft's in-preview native Go compiler ("Project Corsa") — explicitly incomplete (no declaration emit, no `--build` mode, unfinished editor tooling), not production-ready. Both are real tech debt, deliberately not rushed without a dedicated migration/test cycle. tsc clean, vitest 260/260 (34 files, 6 new), lint clean (612 files), guard:design clean, production build succeeds. **Not runtime-verified against a live DB** (same sandbox limitation as every schema-touching row before this one) — the migration SQL needs to actually run against production before `pinnedStats`/the vetting extension take effect; recommend a smoke test on a real profile once deployed. | PATCH /api/profile-editor (pinnedStats field), POST /api/artist-media (vetting extended to all uploads, no new endpoint) | ✅ Done (code) |

| 206 | src/components/FollowButton.tsx, src/app/artists/[slug]/page.tsx, src/app/venues/[slug]/page.tsx, src/app/promoters/[slug]/page.tsx, src/app/fans/[slug]/page.tsx | **Fixed misaligned hero action buttons on mobile (user-reported with screenshot, 2026-07-13: "Doesn't line up. Check for other mobile friendly issues").** Screenshot showed the Artist page's "+ Follow" button wrapping onto two lines ("+" / "Follow") while its siblings (Share, Customize, Settings) stayed single-line, breaking the row's alignment. Root cause was two compounding bugs, both present on Artist and Venue (and a milder form on the DJ/Promoters and Fan pages): **(1)** `FollowButton` and `ShareButton` are shared components dropped into each profile's hero-actions row alongside page-local `Link` buttons (`.artist-hero-btn` etc.) — but `FollowButton` styled itself entirely inline (7px padding, 11px font, pill radius 7) and `ShareButton` defaulted to the unrelated global `.button.small.secondary` class, so the row mixed three incompatible button systems with different heights/radii/fonts. **(2)** The mobile media query forced every child to `flex: 1; min-width: 0` with no `white-space: nowrap`, splitting the row into equal-width slots regardless of content — "+ Follow" (the only multi-word label) was the first to overflow its slot and wrap internally. Fixed by giving `FollowButton` an opt-in `variant="hero"` prop (matches the exact padding/radius/font-size every `*-hero-btn` class already uses; the other 6 call sites — RadioHome, PagesHome ×2, Discover, and the two default-branch fan/DJ usages — keep the original compact chip style, unchanged) and passing an explicit `className` to `ShareButton` on Artist/Fans so it matches too. Replaced the equal-flex mobile rule on Artist/Venue with the same non-wrapping horizontal-scroll pattern their own `.artist-tabs`/`.venue-tabs` already use correctly (`flex-shrink: 0; white-space: nowrap` + `overflow-x: auto`) — matches the original `Artist.dc.html`/`Venue.dc.html` design intent (`flex-wrap:nowrap; overflow-x:auto`), which the live translation had drifted from. DJ/Fan hero rows don't have the forced equal-width rule (they wrap to a second line instead of squeezing text), so the `variant="hero"` fix alone resolves them; left their mobile CSS untouched. tsc clean, vitest 254/254, lint clean, guard:design clean, production build succeeds. **Not screenshot-verified against a live render** — this sandbox has no DB connection to render real profile data; the fix is a straightforward CSS/prop change reasoned through against the exact markup and stylesheet, recommend a quick mobile-viewport check once deployed. | — (UI/CSS only, no API change) | ✅ Done (code) |
| 205 | src/middleware.ts, next.config.mjs, scripts/lint-source.mjs, src/lib/auth.config.ts, src/lib/csp-nonce.ts, CLAUDE.md | **Sitewide issue audit (2026-07-13, requested: "Audit site for issues") — plus a CI-caught revert of this row's own first attempt.** Full health sweep: `tsc --noEmit` clean, `vitest run` 254/254, `guard:design` clean, source-policy `lint` clean, `npm audit --omit=dev` 0 vulnerabilities (the 17 moderate dev-only `@opentelemetry` advisories under Sentry/lighthouse are the same pre-assessed, no-fix-available ones from row 191/192 — not new), production build succeeds. Checked for dead internal links (`href="/..."` and template-literal hrefs against the real route tree) — none found. Checked all 6 `dangerouslySetInnerHTML` call sites — all safe (static content, the existing `toSafeJsonLdString()` sanitizer, or an opaque Prisma-generated ID, never raw user text). **Tried and reverted:** the production build emitted `"middleware" file convention is deprecated. Please use 'proxy' instead"`. First attempt renamed `src/middleware.ts` → `src/proxy.ts` per the official codemod (mechanical: file + default export name, `config`/matcher unchanged) — locally, `tsc`/`vitest`/`lint`/`guard:design`/`next build` all stayed green, so it looked safe and was pushed as PR #505. **CI's workerd-smoke job caught what local checks couldn't:** `ERROR Node.js middleware is not currently supported. Consider switching to Edge Middleware.` Root cause (confirmed via Next.js's own proxy.js docs): `middleware.ts` always defaulted to the Edge runtime; Next.js 16's `proxy.ts` convention **defaults to the Node.js runtime instead**, and critically "the `runtime` config option is not available in Proxy files — setting it will throw an error," so there's no way to opt back into Edge from a `proxy.ts` file. This project deploys to Cloudflare Workers via `@opennextjs/cloudflare`, which does not support Node.js-runtime middleware — hence the CI failure. **Reverted the rename in full** (file, function name, the `scripts/lint-source.mjs` CSP/nonce check that reads it by path, and all comment references in `next.config.mjs`/`auth.config.ts`/`csp-nonce.ts`) and added an explicit **"do not rename to proxy.ts"** note with the reason to `CLAUDE.md`'s critical-backend-wiring table, so a future session doesn't reattempt this and hit the same CI break — the deprecation warning is a known, accepted cost until OpenNext/Cloudflare adds Node.js-runtime middleware support. **Also spot-checked and ruled out as issues:** several undocumented-in-CLAUDE.md routes (`/this-weekend`, `/for-you`, `/journal`, `/community`, `/status`, `/launch`, etc.) are all real, populated pages, not dead stubs — just missing from the page-map table (a documentation gap, not a functional one); an a11y grep for icon-only buttons flagged `MobileQuickGrid.tsx`'s search button, but it renders a visible `{searchPlaceholder}` label alongside the icon — false positive, not an issue. | — (no net route/API change; middleware.ts unchanged from before this row) | ✅ Done (code) — audit clean, attempted fix reverted after CI caught a real incompatibility |
| 204 | src/app/beta/page.tsx, src/app/studio/page.tsx, CLAUDE.md | **"Do all" follow-up to row 203's audit (2026-07-13): retired the design-orphaned Beta page + fixed CLAUDE.md's stale page map.** Beta.dc.html was deleted from Claude Design mid-session (present when row 202/203 fetched it earlier this session, 404 on re-check) — same pattern as its prior deletion (rows 59/65). ---

## Quick Commands for Claude Code

```bash
# Pull latest design files from this project
# (Claude Design exports; Claude Code imports)

# 1. Check what changed
cat DESIGN_SYNC.md | grep "⏳ Pending"

# 2. View the design page
open https://claude.ai/projects/[project-id]/[page].dc.html

# 3. Implement + commit
git add src/app/[route]/page.tsx
git commit -m "sync: implement [page] from design — DESIGN_SYNC #[n]"
git push origin main

# 4. Verify live
open https://ihype.org/[route]

# 5. Mark done in DESIGN_SYNC.md
# Change ⏳ Pending → ✅ [commit SHA]
```
